      <p>
       <b>
        Galician-Asturian
       </b>
       or
       <b>
        Eonavian
       </b>
       (official name by Act 1/1998, March 23 of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Principality_of_Asturias" title="Principality of Asturias">
        Principality of Asturias
       </a>
       ;
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-3">
         [3]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/Exonym_and_endonym" title="Exonym and endonym">
        autonym
       </a>
       :
       <i>
        eonaviego, gallego-asturiano
       </i>
       ;
       <a href="/wiki/Asturian_language" title="Asturian language">
        Asturian
       </a>
       :
       <i>
        <span lang="ast" xml:lang="ast">
         eonaviegu, gallego-asturianu
        </span>
       </i>
       ;
       <a href="/wiki/Galician_language" title="Galician language">
        Galician
       </a>
       :
       <i>
        <span lang="gl" xml:lang="gl">
         eonaviego, galego-asturiano
        </span>
       </i>
       ) is a set of
       <a href="/wiki/Romance_languages" title="Romance languages">
        Romance
       </a>
       dialects or
       <i>
        falas
       </i>
       whose linguistic dominion extends into the zone of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Principality_of_Asturias" title="Principality of Asturias">
        Asturias
       </a>
       between the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eo_River" title="Eo River">
        Eo River
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Navia_River" title="Navia River">
        Navia River
       </a>
       (or more specifically the Eo and the
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Frejulfe_River&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Frejulfe River (page does not exist)">
        Frejulfe River
       </a>
       ). The dialects have been variously classified as the northeastern varieties of
       <a href="/wiki/Galician_language" title="Galician language">
        Galician
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-4">
         [4]
        </a>
       </sup>
       as a linguistic group of its own,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5">
        <a href="#cite_note-5">
         [5]
        </a>
       </sup>
       or as a Galician dialect of transition to the Astur-Leonese group.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6">
        <a href="#cite_note-6">
         [6]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The area where the dialects are spoken includes the Asturian municipalities of
       <a href="/wiki/Boal" title="Boal">
        Boal
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Castropol" title="Castropol">
        Castropol
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Coa%C3%B1a" title="Coaña">
        Coaña
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eilao" title="Eilao">
        Eilao
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/El_Franco" title="El Franco">
        El Franco
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Grandas_de_Salime" title="Grandas de Salime">
        Grandas de Salime
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pez%C3%B3s" title="Pezós">
        Pezós
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/San_Mart%C3%ADn_de_Ozcos" title="San Martín de Ozcos">
        San Martín de Ozcos
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Santalla_de_Ozcos" title="Santalla de Ozcos">
        Santalla de Ozcos
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Santiso_de_Abres" title="Santiso de Abres">
        Santiso de Abres
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Tapia_de_Casariego" title="Tapia de Casariego">
        Tapia de Casariego
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Taramundi" title="Taramundi">
        Taramundi
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Vegadeo" title="Vegadeo">
        A Veiga
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vilanova_de_Ozcos" title="Vilanova de Ozcos">
        Vilanova de Ozcos
       </a>
       , and partially those of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Navia_(Spain)" title="Navia (Spain)">
        Navia
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Ibias" title="Ibias">
        Ibias
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Villay%C3%B3n" title="Villayón">
        Villayón
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Allande" title="Allande">
        Allande
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Other terms used include
       <i>
        gallego-asturiano
       </i>
       , the official term in Asturias,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7">
        <a href="#cite_note-7">
         [7]
        </a>
       </sup>
       meaning "Galician-Asturian language",
       <i>
        a fala
       </i>
       ("the speech", not to be confused with the
       <a href="/wiki/Fala_language" title="Fala language">
        Fala language
       </a>
       of
       <a href="/wiki/Extremadura" title="Extremadura">
        Extremadura
       </a>
       ) and
       <i>
        Galego de Asturias
       </i>
       ("Galician language of Asturias"). The term
       <i>
        Eonaviego
       </i>
       was first used by the linguist Xavier Frías Conde, who translated it as
       <i>
        Eonavian
       </i>
       in English,
       <i>
        Éonavien
       </i>
       in French, and
       <i>
        Eonavienc
       </i>
       in Catalan. In 2007, the
       <a href="/wiki/Academy_of_the_Asturian_Language" title="Academy of the Asturian Language">
        Academy of the Asturian Language
       </a>
       accepted the term
       <i>
        Eonavian
       </i>
       to refer to the
       <a href="/wiki/Galician-Portuguese" title="Galician-Portuguese">
        Galician-Portuguese
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Dialect" title="Dialect">
        dialect
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       The set of dialects was traditionally included by linguists as Galician-Portuguese or
       <a href="/wiki/Galician_language" title="Galician language">
        Galician
       </a>
       , with some characteristics of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Astur-Leonese_Group" title="Astur-Leonese Group">
        Astur-Leonese Group
       </a>
       . That was the opinion of such linguists as
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Men%C3%A9ndez_Pidal" title="Menéndez Pidal">
        Menéndez Pidal
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8">
        <a href="#cite_note-8">
         [8]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eugenio_Coseriu" title="Eugenio Coseriu">
        Eugenio Coseriu
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Lu%C3%ADs_Lindley_Cintra" title="Luís Lindley Cintra">
        Luís Lindley Cintra
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9">
        <a href="#cite_note-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/D%C3%A1maso_Alonso" title="Dámaso Alonso">
        Dámaso Alonso
       </a>
       , and more recent ones such as
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Francisco_Xavier_Fr%C3%ADas_Conde&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Francisco Xavier Frías Conde (page does not exist)">
        Francisco Xavier Frías Conde
       </a>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10">
        <a href="#cite_note-10">
         [10]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Xo%C3%A1n_Babarro&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Xoán Babarro (page does not exist)">
        Xoán Babarro
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11">
        <a href="#cite_note-11">
         [11]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Now, however, there is a political-linguistic conflict on the identity of the language between those who prioritise the mixed identity and those that continue to prioritise the Galician
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Substratum" title="Substratum">
        substratum
       </a>
       . Supporters of the former, mostly in Asturias, identify Eonavian as a
       <a href="/wiki/Dialect_continuum" title="Dialect continuum">
        dialect continuum
       </a>
       between the Asturian and Galician languages or even a third language belonging to
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Portuguese-Galician" title="Portuguese-Galician">
        Portuguese-Galician
       </a>
       group spoken only in that area (Ruth González Rodríguez, Ricardo Saavedra Fernández-Combarro and Xoxé Miguel Suárez).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12">
        <a href="#cite_note-12">
         [12]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Supporters of the latter, mostly in Galicia, identify it as Galician and want the same protection as Galician in
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Castile_and_Leon" title="Castile and Leon">
        Castile and Leon
       </a>
       , which protects the dialects of
       <a href="/wiki/El_Bierzo" title="El Bierzo">
        El Bierzo
       </a>
       in cooperation with the Galician government.
      </p>
      <p>
      </p>

      <p>

      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Classification">
        Classification
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Galician-Asturian&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Classification">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Asturian_linguistic_areas.PNG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="824" data-file-width="993" height="207" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Asturian_linguistic_areas.PNG/250px-Asturian_linguistic_areas.PNG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Asturian_linguistic_areas.PNG/375px-Asturian_linguistic_areas.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Asturian_linguistic_areas.PNG/500px-Asturian_linguistic_areas.PNG 2x" width="250"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Asturian_linguistic_areas.PNG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Linguistic areas of Asturias, attending only to scientific criteria. In green, Asturogalician languages and in purple, Asturoleonese languages
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       From a philological point of view, the origin of the language is surely in the
       <a href="/wiki/Galician-Portuguese" title="Galician-Portuguese">
        Galician-Portuguese
       </a>
       language family, the dominant language in the northwest of the Iberian peninsula in the
       <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">
        Middle Ages
       </a>
       . That follows from an examination of the more than six hundred parchments preserved in the
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Monastery_of_Villanueva_de_Oscos&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Monastery of Villanueva de Oscos (page does not exist)">
        monastery of Villanueva de Oscos
       </a>
       . An examination of the documents of the monastery, written from the late 12th to early 14th centuries, show a certain identity between this language and the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Galician-Portuguese_language" title="Galician-Portuguese language">
        Galician-Portuguese language
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">
        <a href="#cite_note-13">
         [13]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       For the early stage, there are only documented translations of copies of ancient Latin deeds that were beginning to be unintelligible to the common people, (v. AHN sec. clergy, carp. 1617, AHN, Sec Clergy, carp. No. 1617. 15, no. 2, Sec AHN clergy carp. 1621 No 15 etc.), and there would not be until the mid-13th century that the first original deeds were written in the Galician-Portuguese language. In the early 14th century, the oddness of this language with the rest of the galacoifonía, was noticed. The most of these developments were the result of the Castilian language advancement in the urban centres of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/River_Eo" title="River Eo">
        River Eo
       </a>
       :
       <a href="/wiki/Revoredo" title="Revoredo">
        Revoredo
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Ribadeo" title="Ribadeo">
        Ribadeo
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Castropol" title="Castropol">
        Castropol
       </a>
       , such influence was more significant in the writings of the bishops' notaries of Oviedo in these villages, but if the influence of Castilian was growing in the urban centres, the manuscripts of the monastery notaries still kept the original features of this language, and others were added that then appeared.
      </p>
      <p>
       The cartulary of Oscos is an essential landmark for understanding the evolution of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Galician-Portuguese_language" title="Galician-Portuguese language">
        Galician-Portuguese language
       </a>
       , but the monastery's influence was ended with the arrival of the Castillian congregation in 1511. That started another period of great economic and social growth of the monastery around the iron industries, but the installation of the reformed order ended the written language, until its re-emergence in the late 19th century.
      </p>

         audire

       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/%CA%8E" title="ʎ">
        ʎ
       </a>
       : Porcia River to Navia River. The lateral sound
       <a href="/wiki/L" title="L">
        l
       </a>
       : Eo River to Porcia River.
      </p>

      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Phonology">
        Phonology
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Galician-Asturian&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Phonology">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Vowels">
        Vowels
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Galician-Asturian&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Vowels">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Vocalismo_galego_t%C3%B3nico.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="259" data-file-width="755" height="86" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Vocalismo_galego_t%C3%B3nico.jpg/250px-Vocalismo_galego_t%C3%B3nico.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Vocalismo_galego_t%C3%B3nico.jpg/375px-Vocalismo_galego_t%C3%B3nico.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Vocalismo_galego_t%C3%B3nico.jpg/500px-Vocalismo_galego_t%C3%B3nico.jpg 2x" width="250"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Vocalismo_galego_t%C3%B3nico.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Vowel system in Eonavian.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The system of stressed vowels is similar to
       <a href="/wiki/Galician_language" title="Galician language">
        Galician
       </a>
       since there are seven in both languages; it was used by
       <a href="/wiki/Ram%C3%B3n_Men%C3%A9ndez_Pidal" title="Ramón Menéndez Pidal">
        Ramón Menéndez Pidal
       </a>
       when he assigned this language to the group of Galician-Portuguese languages
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16">
        <a href="#cite_note-16">
         [16]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The system is very stable. It does not find the alterations that can be observed by effects of
       <a href="/wiki/Metaphony_(Romance_languages)" title="Metaphony (Romance languages)">
        metaphony
       </a>
       in other regions of Galician phonetics.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">
        <a href="#cite_note-17">
         [17]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Vocalismo_galego_%C3%A1tono.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="201" data-file-width="750" height="67" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Vocalismo_galego_%C3%A1tono.jpg/250px-Vocalismo_galego_%C3%A1tono.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Vocalismo_galego_%C3%A1tono.jpg/375px-Vocalismo_galego_%C3%A1tono.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Vocalismo_galego_%C3%A1tono.jpg/500px-Vocalismo_galego_%C3%A1tono.jpg 2x" width="250"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Vocalismo_galego_%C3%A1tono.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Unstressed vowels in Eonavian.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Here are the vowels obtained by García García in the
       <a href="/wiki/El_Franco" title="El Franco">
        El Franco
       </a>
       village (GG, 1976) and Fernández Vior in
       <a href="/wiki/Vegadeo" title="Vegadeo">
        Vegadeo
       </a>
       (FV ,1997):
      </p>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <dl>
         <dd>
          • ä
          <a href="/wiki/Open_central_unrounded_vowel" title="Open central unrounded vowel">
           Open central unrounded vowel
          </a>
          : f1 =700 y f2 =1350 hz (FV); f1 =750 y f2 =1500 hz (GG)
          <dl>
           <dd>
            – a:
            <a href="/wiki/Open_front_unrounded_vowel" title="Open front unrounded vowel">
             Long open central unrounded vowel
            </a>
            : f1 =870 y f2 =1463 hz (FV); f1 =800 y f2 =1537 hz (GG)
           </dd>
           <dd>
            – a
            <a href="/wiki/Open_front_unrounded_vowel" title="Open front unrounded vowel">
             Open front unrounded vowel
            </a>
            : f1 =700 y f2 =1300 hz (FV); f1 =715 hz y f2 =1400 hz (GG)
           </dd>
           <dd>
            – ɑ
            <a href="/wiki/Open_back_unrounded_vowel" title="Open back unrounded vowel">
             Open back unrounded vowel
            </a>
            ):
           </dd>
          </dl>
         </dd>
         <dd>
          • e
          <a href="/wiki/Close-mid_front_unrounded_vowel" title="Close-mid front unrounded vowel">
           Close-mid front unrounded vowel
          </a>
          : f1 =450 hz y f2 =1900 hz (FV)
          <dl>
           <dd>
            – e Close-mid front unrounded vowel affected by front sound: f1 =475 hz y f2 =1700 hz (GG)
           </dd>
           <dd>
            – e Close-mid front unrounded vowel affected by back sound: f1 =525 hz y f2 =1800 hz (GG)
           </dd>
          </dl>
         </dd>
         <dd>
          • ɛ
          <a href="/wiki/Open-mid_front_unrounded_vowel" title="Open-mid front unrounded vowel">
           Open-mid front unrounded vowel
          </a>
          : f1 =700 hz y f2 =1800 hz (FV)
         </dd>
         <dd>
          • o
          <a href="/wiki/Close-mid_back_rounded_vowel" title="Close-mid back rounded vowel">
           Close-mid back rounded vowel
          </a>
          : f1 =490 y f2 =1015 (FV); f1 =500 y f2=1075 (GG)
         </dd>
         <dd>
          • ɔ
          <a href="/wiki/Open-mid_back_rounded_vowel" title="Open-mid back rounded vowel">
           Open-mid back rounded vowel
          </a>
          : f1 =555 hz y f2 =1100 (FV): f1 =600 hz y f2 =1100 hz (GG)
         </dd>
         <dd>
          • i
          <a href="/wiki/Close_front_unrounded_vowel" title="Close front unrounded vowel">
           Close front unrounded vowel
          </a>
          : f1 =337 y f2 =2300 (FV); f1 =400 y f2 =2600 hz (GG)
         </dd>
         <dd>
          • u
          <a href="/wiki/Close_back_rounded_vowel" title="Close back rounded vowel">
           Close back rounded vowel
          </a>
          : f1 =350 y f1 =1185 (FV); f1 =400 y f2 =925 hz (GG)
         </dd>
        </dl>
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <p>
       As it was indicated by García García regarding unstressed vowels, "Unlike other areas of Galician phonetics, there are no relevant differences between open and closed
       <i>
        -e-
       </i>
       and
       <i>
        -o-
       </i>
       and the sound of variant pairs can be considered, each with their own
       <i>
        archiphonemes
       </i>
       , keeping the following system: -i-, E-, a,-O-, u.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18">
        <a href="#cite_note-18">
         [18]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Vocalismo_galego_%C3%A1tono_final.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="169" data-file-width="691" height="61" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Vocalismo_galego_%C3%A1tono_final.jpg/250px-Vocalismo_galego_%C3%A1tono_final.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Vocalismo_galego_%C3%A1tono_final.jpg/375px-Vocalismo_galego_%C3%A1tono_final.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Vocalismo_galego_%C3%A1tono_final.jpg/500px-Vocalismo_galego_%C3%A1tono_final.jpg 2x" width="250"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Vocalismo_galego_%C3%A1tono_final.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Unstressed vowels in final position
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       There are three unstressed vowels in final position: -e-,-o-and-a -.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19">
        <a href="#cite_note-19">
         [19]
        </a>
       </sup>
       There is the loss of the
       <i>
        -o
       </i>
       endings
       <i>
        -ene
       </i>
       and
       <i>
        -inu
       </i>
       , ‘sen’, ‘fren’, ‘centen’, 'allén', ‘padrín’, ‘camín’..., an overall conservation "-e" syllables end, after ‘-ete’ and ‘ite’ headquarters, 'rede', 'vide', 'parede', etc... It is clearer still in place names ‘San Mamede’, ‘Nonide’, ‘Taladride’. It is also normal to conserve "-e" after "θ" like in ‘couce, 'fouce', etc. On the other hand, under the influence of Castilian, ‘salú’, ‘verdá’, ‘enfermedá’, it has been lost The paragogic vowel -e- after liquids consonant appear very residually, Acevedo y Huelves cites ‘carcele’. Final vowel -o- has disappeared in suffix -elo, in toponyms: ‘Tol’, ‘Castropol’, ‘Boal’, etc.
      </p>
      <p>
       Until the 19th century, nasal vowels were a fairly common phenomenon throughout Eonaviego but today arw very unusual.
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Damaso_Alonso" title="Damaso Alonso">
        Damaso Alonso
       </a>
       was the first in confirming the phenomenon, widespread in the nearby Ancares Mountains. M. Menéndez García finds nasality remains in Freixulfe and points in Villallón Village, y Celso Muñiz in the Valledor region, in the frontier with the Asturo-Leonese languages. These remnants of nasal vowels in Eonavian explain that the syllables ended in nasal coda are always opened, the necessary consequence of velarization, the stage prior to the formation of the nasal.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20">
        <a href="#cite_note-20">
         [20]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       A change in unstressed vowels when absolute enclitic position has labial consonant and vowel assimilation.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">
        <a href="#cite_note-21">
         [21]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Regarding the unstressed vowels, as pointed out by García García, "Unlike other areas of the Galaicofonía, the relevant differences between open e-y-o and closed sounds can be considered such as variants of two separate couples archiphoneme, keeping to the following system-i-, E-, a,-O-, u.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22">
        <a href="#cite_note-22">
         [22]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       As is clearly evident by García García, the nasalization of vowels preceding tonic or atonic to ensure –n- in coda "tamen", or situated between nasal consonants "mañá". Vowel lengthening occurs as a result by contractions: "vou à casa" or by compensation as a result of the loss of intervocalic nasal "machacan a 'llá/lá
       <i>
        ", "Que
       </i>
       mañá' nos traiga un
       <i>
        bó
       </i>
       día de solín".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23">
        <a href="#cite_note-23">
         [23]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The extension is also in the case of concomitant vowels, like in the proverb "A terra que da á ortiga".
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Diphthongs">
        Diphthongs
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Galician-Asturian&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Diphthongs">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Falling diphthong
        <i>
         : 'couto', 'souto', 'cantou', 'deitou', 'cantei'...
        </i>
       </li>
       <li>
        Anticipation of the "yod", like
        <i>
         : 'naide', 'coiro', 'agoiro', 'cadeira'...
        </i>
       </li>
       <li>
        No nasal diphthong at the end, as noted by Menendez Garcia as one of the benchmark isoglosses the speeches and Asturleonesas Galaicas.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24">
         <a href="#cite_note-24">
          [24]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Semivowels">
        Semivowels
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Galician-Asturian&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Semivowels">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Unlike Galician-Portuguese and Portuguese, Eonavian, like Galician, tends to the abolition of semiconsonants, but it has evolved its own way, linked to treatment of
        <a href="/wiki/Nasalization" title="Nasalization">
         nasality
        </a>
        , such as the relative articles ‘condo’, ‘contó’ or the toponyms 'Sayane' (Saint John) and the names 'Xan'(John, 'Xanón' (Big John) etc…
       </li>
       <li>
        In Eonaviego, as in the rest of the Galaicofonía, is a tendency to anticipatory assimilation, but today, both Eonaviego and Gallego have a strong influence from Castilian. In both cases, the process does not extend beyond the influence by it: 'naide', 'beizo', 'coiro', 'caldeiro', 'ribeira', etc...
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Nasal_consonants">
        Nasal consonants
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Galician-Asturian&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Nasal consonants">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Galician_linguistic_areas.PNG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1308" data-file-width="1485" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Galician_linguistic_areas.PNG/250px-Galician_linguistic_areas.PNG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Galician_linguistic_areas.PNG/375px-Galician_linguistic_areas.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Galician_linguistic_areas.PNG/500px-Galician_linguistic_areas.PNG 2x" width="250"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Galician_linguistic_areas.PNG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Map about Galician-Portuguese speaking areas taking into account principally the nasality factor. Map based on Fernández Rei's outline, "Dialectoloxía da lingua galega".
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Intervocalic vowels are lost. That fact is the argument of greater weight to those opposed to the theory of Astur-Galician, precisely because there is the curious fact that the phenomenon is accentuated in the municipalities close to the probable Eonaviegos West following a north-south trend is started in
        <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">
         Portugal
        </a>
        . The fact is manifested in the formation of plurals, on increases in the training of women, but especially in the loss of the nasal-palatal.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25">
         <a href="#cite_note-25">
          [25]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        The velarization of nasal vowels and deformation from n-falling.
        <a href="/wiki/D%C3%A1maso_Alonso" title="Dámaso Alonso">
         Dámaso Alonso
        </a>
        , «Engañar, volar, casos y resultados de velariación de –n- en el dominio Gallego».
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26">
         <a href="#cite_note-26">
          [26]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        The evolution of group Latin nn &gt; n.
       </li>
       <li>
        The retention of -mb-.
       </li>
       <li>
        The group m’l y m’n changes to m
       </li>
       <li>
        The loss of nasal-palatals, in diminutive feminine, vaquía, cousía, roupía, etc. and some masculines foucío, campío, en el sufijo -ieiro/a: cocieira, dieiro, mulieiro, etc.
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Lateral_consonants">
        <a href="/wiki/Lateral_consonant" title="Lateral consonant">
         Lateral consonants
        </a>
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Galician-Asturian&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Lateral consonants">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <ul>
       <li>
        The retention of intervocalic lateral consonants: except in the most western counties, the trend is the maintenance of intervocalic -l, except in the
        <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Cartulary_of_Villanueva_de_Oscos_Monastery&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Cartulary of Villanueva de Oscos Monastery (page does not exist)">
         cartulary of Villanueva de Oscos Monastery
        </a>
        the tendency to the disappearance of the intervocalic -l- is like the rest of the Galician-Portuguese languages.
       </li>
       <li>
        The palatalization of the initial lateral and degemination absence of Latin "-ll-". Now, it occurs inonly half the territory, but the examination of the Cartulary de Oscos confirm that this phenomenon was widespread in all Galician and Asturian counties from the
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/River_Eo" title="River Eo">
         River Eo
        </a>
        and the
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Navia_River" title="Navia River">
         Navia River
        </a>
        . (See García Leal, "En los Albores del Asturiano (II). «La palatización de la -l- inicial en la documentación latina altomedieval del Reino Astur-leonés», (718-1037).
       </li>
       <li>
        The velarization of "B'D" (cold, Dold, etc.), is now a very rare a phenomenon and absent from Huelves Acevedo García, who reported "coldo" and "codo", but it was widespread in the Oscos.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27">
         <a href="#cite_note-27">
          [27]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Evolution_of_the_Latin_groups">
        Evolution of the Latin groups
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Galician-Asturian&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Evolution of the Latin groups">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <ul>
       <li>
        The evolution -cl-, -pl- y -fl- to palatal dull sound is agreed about in western Bable and Galician since "che vaqueira" tends to be more fricative (š) than affricate (ć).
       </li>
       <li>
        The group -lt-, -ct- and -sc- evolved to it and ix.
       </li>
       <li>
        The gj, gi, j, nj, li, gl were palatised.
       </li>
       <li>
        The ss evolved to a palatal, dull fricative.
       </li>
       <li>
        The gy, -dy-, -sc- evolved to a palatal dull fricative.
       </li>
       <li>
        Liquid consonants after occlusives changed to vocalic sounds: oculu &gt; òyo, vetulu &gt; vèyo, apicula &gt; abeya, tegula &gt; tèya, flagrare &gt; cheirar, agru &gt; eiro, cathedra &gt; cadèira.
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Other_phenomena">
        Other phenomena
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Galician-Asturian&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Other phenomena">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Fricative occlusives became sharper than Asturian, even more than in Galician: 'louxa', 'vixo', 'dexobado', 'xardía', 'broxa', 'xebrar', 'xastre', 'ameixola', 'èixola'.
       </li>
       <li>
        Palatalization to letter x.
       </li>
       <li>
        Distinction between palatals, fricatives and laterals. García García proposes the following oppositions: 'callo' ('callar' verb), cayo ('caer' verb), rayo (meteorological phenomenon), rallo ('rallar' verb), etc.
       </li>
       <li>
        Neutralization of liquid pool, but that phenomenon is on the verge of disappearance.
       </li>
       <li>
        Retention of Latin -f-.
       </li>
       <li>
        Geminate ss evolved to a fricative: Latin
        <i>
         passaru
        </i>
        &gt; Eonavian
        <i>
         páxaro
        </i>
        , Latin
        <i>
         bassare
        </i>
        &gt; Eonavian
        <i>
         baxar
        </i>
        , etc.
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Morphology">
        Morphology
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Galician-Asturian&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Morphology">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Verbs">
        Verbs
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Galician-Asturian&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Verbs">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <b>
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tenses" title="Tenses">
          Verbal tenses
         </a>
        </b>
        : indicative present, imperfect, perfect, pluperfect simple, conditional future; subjunctive present and imperfect; Imperative, infinitive simple and conjugate, participle and gerund.
       </li>
       <li>
        The
        <b>
         synthetic future
        </b>
        the construction of the future tense is with the phrase verb 'haber' + pronoun + tense infinitive: "eiyes atizar" u otras "eivos dar", "y'a poñer", which are similar to others used in Galician-Portuguese to prioritise the personal pronoun to the desinence ending: atizaryes-ei, darvos-ei, poñerlle-a.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28">
         <a href="#cite_note-28">
          [28]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        The
        <b>
         conjugated infinitive
        </b>
        is used subordinate constructions if the infinitive ends or is part of a prepositional phrase; processes have different subjects and aims to avoid ambiguity.
       </li>
       <li>
        Like the rest of the family
        <a href="/wiki/Galician-Portuguese" title="Galician-Portuguese">
         Galician-Portuguese
        </a>
        , there is a strong dependence of original vocalism in Latin, and in Galician-Asturian, it is even more conservative. The verbal inflection of Eonavian is conditioned by the loss of the distinction between open and closed vowels in Vulgar Latin. The disappearance of the distinction between unstressed vowels made the mobility of stressed vowels within the verbal root make morpheme prevail over the root in most cases, distinguishing between open and closed position as tonic when it was combined.
       </li>
      </ul>
      <p>
       Thus, the vowels acquired certain metaphonic connotations, to incorporate the distinction into verbal inflection and ignore the etymological origin of the words. The strong personal forms (the three person singular and third plural present indicative, subjunctive and all of the second imperative) are always distinguished by speakers between vowel -e- and open-o and between the strong and weak of forms other than monosyllabic verbs if the stressed vowel of the root morpheme and the match, except for the verbs given duty and irregular in Galician-Asturian. These are the main features of the verb forms in the language:
      </p>
      <p>
       The –des is in the second person plural of every conjugation. García García confirms that although the ending is maintained stably in the second and third conjugations, in the first conjugation, it is giving way to the influence of Castilian -ais and -aides.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29">
        <a href="#cite_note-29">
         [29]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The perfect past –che has in the first person singular, ‘veño’, ‘teño’, ‘vexo’.
      </p>
      <p>
       There is a vocal deformation by the rizotónic effect.
      </p>
      <p>
       Infinitive ending in -r- join with pronomes.
      </p>
      <p>
       There is a disappearance of –s- in the first person plural to join ‘nos’ enclitic.
      </p>
      <p>
       The -n- paragogic is in the first person singular perfect in all strong and bending double –er, -ir, dixen-, puxen, fun, salin, còmín.
      </p>
      <p>
       Endings in -i often take -n paragójica: tomein, falein, subirein, falarein, hein, sein.
      </p>
      <p>
       The open -e forms in the first person plural past (coyèmos, dixèmos) or the open o- in second and third person plural (fòmos, fòron).
      </p>
      <p>
       The infinitive in –er- in many verbs in Castillian is in -ir: ‘morrer’, ‘encher’, ‘ferver’, ‘render’, etc., less frequently, the form hesitates: ‘valir’/’valer’ y ‘tosir’/’toser’.
      </p>
      <p>
       An alternation occurs -e- open and closed in verbs with-e-open rizotónica for which the -e- radical of the singular and the third person plural.
      </p>
      <p>
       Foe verbs ending in in-cer, the first person singular present indicative and subjunctive present are treated as ces: ce lluzo, lluce, lluza, lluzas, lluza.
      </p>
      <p>
       There is an alternation between open and closed in the thematic vowel tonic of most verbs in -er.
      </p>
      <p>
       Closed -e- is typical for all persons in the plural of the perfect, six of pluperfect simple, all the imperfect subjunctive in the two series, and forms of the gerund and the first person future, in the first and second person plural present, the plural of the imperative of the first and second person plural of the future, both as in the hypothetical future-e.
      </p>
      <p>
       Verbs (medir and sentir) show an alternation i/e in the root vowel: with -i-in the strong forms (forms in the singular and the third plural of the present, the singular imperative and all of the subjunctive) and -e-in the weak vowels.
      </p>
      <p>
       Western Asturian occurs accentuates the first and second persons of the plural present subjunctive.
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Garcia Garcia and Celso Muñiz admit the existence of composite shapes with verb ‘ter’ as an assistant. However, that is more from such an approach particular of the authors on the morphosyntax of the compound forms than as the existence of their own specialty in Eonavian.
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Nouns">
        Nouns
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Galician-Asturian&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Nouns">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <ul>
       <li>
        The
        <a href="/wiki/Gender" title="Gender">
         gender
        </a>
        and the
        <a href="/wiki/Number" title="Number">
         number
        </a>
        are o/a, os/as. These forms are altered the loss of intervolcalic -n-: ratois (mice), caxois (drawers).
       </li>
       <li>
        The instability of nasal consonants alters also augmentatives and diminutives:
        <i>
         casúa
        </i>
        (big house), pedrúa (big stones), casía (small house), pedría (small stone), etc.
       </li>
       <li>
        It is also characteristic of Eonavian to change gender to specify a group or an unknown number of things: "el anada", "el herba", ("a herba" a blade of grass, "el hierba", a grass farod) and in adverbial locutions to "da feito" (in fact), "da remoyo" (soacking), etc.
       </li>
       <li>
        Although the forms of gender-neutral are widespread, highlighted by Frías Conde, the use of the forms is from the influence of Castilian, and the forms used to be unknown in Eonavian («Los derivados de "ille" e "illum" en el gallego de Asturias», Revista de Filología Románica, nº 10, 1993, pp. 241–252), so it is strange that it is precisely the neutral "lo", the only article that begins in a consonant, it is beyond question it is
        <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">
         [
         <i>
          <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify">
           <span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (January 2017)">
            clarification needed
           </span>
          </a>
         </i>
         ]
        </sup>
        that no analyst records the existence of contractions with -lo', something unacceptable in Galician and Asturian.
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Syntax">
        Syntax
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Galician-Asturian&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Syntax">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Pronouns">
        Pronouns
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Galician-Asturian&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Pronouns">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <ul>
       <li>
        The Latin vocalism of the first-person pronoun, albeit with different embodiments, is retained: èu/èo.
       </li>
       <li>
        There is a general extension of prepositional contractions of a similar nature. Contractions of unstressed pronouns, accusative dative are used more: mo, ma, mas, cho, cha, chas, yo, yos, yas.
       </li>
       <li>
        The accusative and the dative in the personal pronouns are distinguished: the second person is te/che, the third person ye/lo/la. Pronominal form «min» is always a complement with a preposition: a min, por min, de min, etc.
       </li>
       <li>
        Use of an interest dative: ‘’Eso nun che me gusta nada, vouchéme fer un traxe, llevábachebos un traxe, éche grande, vaiye cansao’’: the pronomes "che"- and –"ye"- have a sympathetic or interest value to highlight the attention of the recipient of the action. However, the indirect object lost the condition when it is preceded by the reflexive indirect object.
       </li>
       <li>
        The lack of reflexive complement.is replaced by different forms: ‘’ye: yo, ya, yos, yas, así: deoyo, llevayo’’, etc.
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Partitives">
        Partitives
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Galician-Asturian&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Partitives">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Retention of prepositional syntagma partitives (accusative partial) in restrictive clauses or specification of content with transitive verbs.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30">
         <a href="#cite_note-30">
          [30]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Prepositions">
        Prepositions
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Galician-Asturian&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Prepositions">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <ul>
       <li>
        A, agá, ante, ata, acía, baxo, cara, con, contra, de, dende, en, entre, escontra, menos, pra, prantre, por, según, sen, xunta, tras/tres.
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Chartulary">
        Chartulary
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Galician-Asturian&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Chartulary">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Monasterio_de_Santa_Mar%C3%ADa_de_Villanueva_de_Oscos_(2796374867).jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="2048" height="188" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Monasterio_de_Santa_Mar%C3%ADa_de_Villanueva_de_Oscos_%282796374867%29.jpg/250px-Monasterio_de_Santa_Mar%C3%ADa_de_Villanueva_de_Oscos_%282796374867%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Monasterio_de_Santa_Mar%C3%ADa_de_Villanueva_de_Oscos_%282796374867%29.jpg/375px-Monasterio_de_Santa_Mar%C3%ADa_de_Villanueva_de_Oscos_%282796374867%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Monasterio_de_Santa_Mar%C3%ADa_de_Villanueva_de_Oscos_%282796374867%29.jpg/500px-Monasterio_de_Santa_Mar%C3%ADa_de_Villanueva_de_Oscos_%282796374867%29.jpg 2x" width="250"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Monasterio_de_Santa_Mar%C3%ADa_de_Villanueva_de_Oscos_(2796374867).jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Monastery of Oscos Apse
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       One of the most relevant aspects of the language is the study of its evolution in the
       <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">
        Middle Ages
       </a>
       through the parchments which are kept in the
       <a href="/wiki/Villanueva_de_Oscos" title="Villanueva de Oscos">
        Villanueva de Oscos
       </a>
       Chartulary, the fourth most important in
       <a href="/wiki/Asturias" title="Asturias">
        Asturias
       </a>
       after San Pelayo, San Vicente and the
       <a href="/wiki/Oviedo_Cathedral" title="Oviedo Cathedral">
        Oviedo Cathedral
       </a>
       . It is very interesting its conservation by the massive information provided a community so small as the Villanueva de Oscos Abbey. The documents show us the vitality of this language in the
       <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">
        Middle Ages
       </a>
       and give very important information on Romance languages in the northwest of
       <a href="/wiki/Iberian_Peninsula" title="Iberian Peninsula">
        Iberian Peninsula
       </a>
       . The Chartulary preserves 616 parchments about the Middle Ages: 32 from the 12th century, 261 from the 13th century, 224 from the 14th century and 99 from the 15th century.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31">
        <a href="#cite_note-31">
         [31]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The first scholar who dealt with its study was Aureliano Fernández-Guerra in 1865, in the very important article «Speech about the Carther of Aviles». He used extracts of 19 documents from 1256 to 1316. In 1868, Martín Sangrador y Vitores included in his work about the Asturias administration a copy in Galician of the royal prerrogative given away by
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fernando_II_of_Portugal" title="Fernando II of Portugal">
        Fernando II
       </a>
       to the Abbey. The next edition of the documents about monastery had to wait until the mid-20th century, when the
       <a href="/wiki/Royal_Institute_of_Asturian_Studies" title="Royal Institute of Asturian Studies">
        Royal Institute of Asturian Studies
       </a>
       (RIDEA) edited the article «El convento benedictino de Villanueva de Ozcos»
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32">
        <a href="#cite_note-32">
         [32]
        </a>
       </sup>
       by Marcos G. Martínez, a rather poor edition. Only in 1981, Pedro Floriano Llorente publishes in RIDEA «Colección dipolomática de Villanueva de Ozcos»,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33">
        <a href="#cite_note-33">
         [33]
        </a>
       </sup>
       which implies an important improvement concerning the previous, both by perfection technical, as by the personal and toponymic references.
      </p>
      <p>
       Nonetheless, the edition dealt with the issue only as far as 1200. In 1994, the Britonia journal published the second serial of the monastery's parchments, edited by Floriano Llorente, covering until the first half of the 13th century. The edition, however, failed to meet the editors' expectations.because no documents were produced in Romance so Britonia published a second version, less known, to covers until 1300, more interesting for the study of the question.
      </p>
      <p>
       The works served as a basis to publish another set of documents by Professor Alvárez Castrillón in his book
       <i>
        Los Ozcos en los siglos X-XIII, un modelo de organización social del espacio en la Asturias medieval
       </i>
       , (2001), but the work addresses only the historic aspects and not the linguistics. In the following years, Professor Sanz Fuentes has published also four other documents with regard to Buron Hospital. Finally, Alvárez Castrillón, edited, in 2008, 605 more parchments as attachments to the book «La Comarca de los Oscos en la Edad Media, poblamiento, economía y poder», and in 2011, he edited 293 more documents from 1139 to 1300,
       <i>
        Colección Diplomática del Monasterio de Santa María de Villanueva de Oscos, (1139-1300)
       </i>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       The documents of the chartulary give important information for knowledge of the language spoken in the western Asturias in the Middle Ages. They show the origin and the evolution of this language, but the serial of parchments finishes with the arrival the
       <a href="/wiki/Congregation_(Catholic)" title="Congregation (Catholic)">
        Congregation
       </a>
       of
       <a href="/wiki/Crown_of_Castile" title="Crown of Castile">
        Castile
       </a>
       in 1511 at Monastery, the end of a cycle and will be the beginning of a new one, the big economic growth around the iron industry. However, the installation of the reformed order closed the documental history of this language, until its resurgence in the late 19th century.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Sample_texts">
        Sample texts
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">

         ]

       <p>

         ...Testo uobis et concedo per suis terminis certis per termino de Menustux e inde de super ad petram de Gio a Cornu de Menyones, et ad penna de Teyxeyra, et al Pico pequeno, et allas mestas de Bouspoulim) et como uay pello regueyro a Sobrepe aa pena das ouellas, et inde in directum ad petra Vocatoria et ad aquam de Ferueça et cómodo uertitur aquam al final de Pena Leyra, na Gauia per ubi potueritis inueniere.... Ad patrem (sic) vero regis quingentos solidos boos exsoluat.
        </i>
       </p>
       <div class="templatequotecite">

        <cite>

          </a>
         </sup>
        </cite>

       (1153)
      </p>
      <blockquote class="templatequote">
       <p>

         Cunusçuda cousa seia a quantos esta carta viren commo eu María Uicentez de Cedamona vendo a uos abbade don Guillermo de Santa María de Villa Noua d’Oscos e ao conueto desse mismo lugar quanta heredade eu aio e deuo auer en Çedamona por preço qua a mí e a uos ben prougo, conuen a saber: hun boy boon e çen solidos, preço me outorgo por ben pagada e sse mays val doo por Deus e por mina alma e de meus parentes. E de este día en deante seia tirada de nosso poder e seia metuda en no uosso e no do moestero e se alzen da mina parte ou da aldea contra esta uençon contra esta doaçon veer, aia a maldiçon de Deus e a mina e con Iudas eno inferno iasca por senpre e aa uoz del rey peyte çen morabentinos e dobre ao moestero a heredade e a carta uala por senpre. Feyta a carta en Gyo...
        </i>
       </p>
       <div class="templatequotecite">
        —
        <cite>
         Floriano Llorente, Pedro.
         <i>
          Coleción diplomática del Monasterio de Villanueva de Oscos
         </i>

         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TA102-06_34-1">

      <p>
       (late 13th century)

      <blockquote class="templatequote">
       <p>
        <i>
         Se vos ende quissierdes yr leyxade a quarta de quanto overdes ao monasterio… a vossa morte venirdes aa septultura do monasterio con vossas mandaciones
        </i>
       </p>
       <div class="templatequotecite">
        —
        <cite>

        </cite>
       </div>
      </blockquote>
      <p>
       (1261)
      </p>
      <blockquote class="templatequote">
       <p>
        <i>
         In dei nomine Amen. Cunnuzuda cousa seia aquantos esta carta viren et oyren. Como nos don Miguel pela gracia de dios Abbade do Monesteyro de Sancta Maria de Vila Noua d’Oscos et ho Conuento dese mismo logar. Damos anos Rodrigo Affonso tam sola mente poren uossos dias emprestamo: amea daquela nossa herdade de vila Donga. Que he ena Vila d’Aures aque tenno de uos Lope Trauesso. Et damos uola todos sous terminos et con todos sous vilares assy comoa nos auemos. Per tal preyto uos damos esta herdade sobredita quela non possades vender nen supinnorar nen enallenar per neguna maneyra et adia de vosso passamento que ffique esta herdade ia dita liure et quita al Monesteyro ia dito con quanto bon paramento enela ouuer.
        </i>
       </p>
       <p>
        Et Eu Rodrigo Affonso ia dito obridome per mi et per todas mias bonas et su pena Mil mrs. de Moeda Real; que nunca esta herdade ia dita meu fillo et filla nen quen vener en mias bonas; que nuncaa embarguen al Monesteyro ia dito. Et se meu fillo ou mia filla aesta carta quiseren passar aian amia maldizion et nunca seian herdados en mia herdade, et peyten al Monesteyro mil moravidiis da moeda real et acarta seia sempre atodo tempo valiosa. Et eu Rodrigo Affonso ia dito; recibo de vos don abade et do Conuento ia dito este prestamo que me vos dades et outorgo ben et lealmente de comprir quanto esta carta diz. Et que esto seia mays ffirme et no possa venir en dolda.
       </p>
       Mandamos ambas las partes ffacer esta carta partida per ABC feyta carta en Vila noua d’Oscos XII dias por andar del mes de Junyo en era de mil et CCC et XIII annos. Regnante el rey don Affonso en Leon en Castela en todos los outros sous Rengos ayglegia de Oviedo porgante. Rodrigo Rodriguiz meyrino mayor del Rey eno Regno de Leon et en Asturias, osque presentes foron Suer Lopez prior testis, Pay Martiniz Suprior testis. Miguel Celareyro testis, Iohan Pelaiz vestiario testis, Pero Fernandiz cantor; testis Petro Iohanes sucantor testis, Andreu Perez clerigo desancta offemena testis, sou parente pero pelaiz clerigo testis, Lope Díaz testis, Meen Perez testis, Pay Eanes testis, Pero Chazin testis Gonzalo caio testis ffernan Díaz fillo de Diego vello testis et outros muytos que viron et oyron et eu Freire Domingo Monniz Notario puplico de Vila Nova d’Oscos scriui esta carta per mandado danbaslas partos et puys enela meusinal
       <div class="templatequotecite">
        <i>
         —
         <cite>
          <a href="/wiki/Aureliano_Fern%C3%A1ndez-Guerra" title="Aureliano Fernández-Guerra">
           Fernández Guerra y Orbe, Aureliano
          </a>
          , Discurso en la Real Academia Española en el aniversario de su fundación, Madrid, 1865, p 84
         </cite>
        </i>
       </div>
      </blockquote>
      <p>
       (12 June 1276)
      </p>
      <blockquote class="templatequote">
       <p>
        <i>
         E por esta doaçión e por esta esmolna que vos Pedro Méndez façedes ao monsterio sobredito e abade e convento que son e que an de de vir, e por cuanto ben e emparamento façedes ao mosterio e prometedes de façer, nos abbade e convento logo de presente reçebemosvos llogo por noso familiar e damosvos e outorgamos parte en todo o ben que se feçer no mosterio de Santa María de Villa Nova en toda a orden de Cistel ata o día da fin do mundo...

         Sepan quantos esta carta viren commo Teresa Meen, frada profesa no Monesterio de Santa María de Villa Nova d'Oscos, do en doazon al dito monesterio, por las almas de meu padre de mina madre e mía, e de aquelos a quen eu son teuda, todos benes asy mobres commo rayzes que eu aio en Lanteyro, en Bullaso, en Lavallos e en Mon, e en todos los terminos e jurdiçon da Probra de Castropol, e otorgo e mando que seian do monesterio todos, por quanto os mandaron y meu padre e mina madre con meu otorgamento. E vos, o dito don Abbad e convento, non me avedes a tirar estos erdamentos nen parte de delos, nen los otros que y el monesterio que levava meu padre e mia madre por los trinta maravedís según teno huna carta per que nos aforastes e dovos liçençia que vos pósades trocar e ministrar por lo dito foro os novos delos. E non avedes a dar nen aforar, nen vender, nen supinnorar, nen allear, nen malparar estos ditos herdamentos e benes. E Eu Teresa Meen frada profesa do dito monesterio asy o otorgo e prometo de ter e gardar todo esto que se aquí reconta.

[Esto] todo asy commo senpre andóu esto commo dito [he vos] aforamos que déades e pagedes de foro en cada hun anno todos los foros e deretos ao convento e [ao moesterio] asy commo pagaua o dito Miguel Andrés e desta erdad que auedes de dar el quarto a Dominga Fernández por seus días muller que foe de Aluaro de Perdigueros...

      </p>
      <blockquote class="templatequote">
       <p>
        <i>
         Lliras che quito, nel marco las poño, toma, can, lliras y pan.
        </i>
        <br/>
       </p>
       <p>
        <i>
         En Villanova nin vaca nin nora nacen os gutos y votanlos fora.
        </i>
        <br/>
        <i>
         En Llanteiro nun hay mozas, en Mezà todas son veyas, en Miñagon milindrosas y en Serandías a fror d'ellas.
        </i>
        <br/>
        <i>
         Pernas tortas das Cavanas, regallóis os da Pilella, chamuscados os de Boal, viva el llugarín de Armal.
        </i>
        <br/>
       </p>
       <i>
        Veite cerzo, cercellín, de este valle regueirín, qu'ei che vèn Xuan de riba, xurando y devotando, que ch'a partir ua dida, si te coye costa arriba, que ch'a partir un brazo si te coye costa abaxo.
       </i>
       <div class="templatequotecite">
        —
        <cite>
         Acevedo Huelves, Boal y su Concejo, Oviedo 1.898 pp. 50, 61 and 76
        </cite>
       </div>
      </blockquote>
      <blockquote class="templatequote">
       <p>
        <i>
         Polavila polavila, Eu ben sei donde la hay, indo porlo río arriba no moliño de meu pay
        </i>
       </p>
       <div class="templatequotecite">
        —
        <cite>
         .Acevedo Huelves, Boal y su Concejo, Oviedo 1.898 p. 76.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35">
          <a href="#cite_note-35">
           [35]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </cite>
       </div>
      </blockquote>
      <p>
       (Villanueva de Oscos)
      </p>
      <blockquote class="templatequote">
       <p>
        <i>
         En casa chía, llougo se fai a cía.
        </i>
        <br/>
        <i>
         Condo che dian a oveya, coye a corda y vay por ella.
        </i>
        <br/>
        <i>
         As cuitas ayías, num me quitan dormir.
        </i>
        <br/>
        <i>
         A mía fiya arruita fame muita, a mía nora vocía e de chía.
        </i>
        <br/>
        <i>
         A terra que da á ortiga è pra mía fiya/, a que nun la cría è pra mía vecía
        </i>
        <br/>
        <i>
         Pra que nun queren, teño èo abondo
        </i>
        <br/>
        <i>
         Antroido, godoiro, paso por Arbon con un cesto na mau comendo rapón.
        </i>
        <br/>
        <i>
         D`os sesenta pra riba, nun moyes a barriga.
        </i>
        <br/>
        <i>
         De valdre texen os cais, que nun rompen a roupa.
        </i>
        <br/>
        <i>
         A vaca da mía vecía, da meyor lleite ca mía.
        </i>
        <br/>
        <i>
         Condo Dios nun quer, os Santos nun poden.
        </i>
        <br/>
        <i>
         Que mañá nos traiga, un boo día de solín.
        </i>
        <br/>
        <i>
         Arco de veya revolve na terra, col dido monín que nun chova por mín, col dido pulgar que chova nel mar.
        </i>
        <br/>
        <i>
         Foyas na figueira, farros na ribeira.
        </i>
        <br/>
        <i>
         Cerco lluar ponte a enxugar.
        </i>
        <br/>
        <i>
         Xente de marina, xente de gran caldeirada, día de muyto víspera de nada.
        </i>
        <br/>
        <i>
         Home fraque y non de fame, mira que nun te agarre.
        </i>
        <br/>
        <i>
         Condo chove y fai frío, cantan os gallos na veira del río.
        </i>
        <br/>
        <i>
         Condo Dios quer, de todos os ventos chove
        </i>
        <br/>
        <i>
         El anada de un mal ano, máyase nun eirado
        </i>
        .
        <br/>
        <i>
         Cantaide nenas, cantaide, /cantaide y nun teñais pena/que ven un barco de mozos/ a dous cuartos á docena
        </i>
        .
        <br/>
        <i>
         Si a Candeleira chora/ el inverno xa vai fora / si a candeleira rí / El inverno ta por vir
        </i>
        <br/>
        <i>
         Alló enriba, nun, sei unde, encontrein con nun sei quen, en casa de xa me esqueice, nun me podo acordar ben.
        </i>
       </p>
       <div class="templatequotecite">
        —
        <cite>
         Fernández Fernández, Marcelino. El Franco y su Concejo, p. 112
        </cite>
       </div>
      </blockquote>
      <blockquote class="templatequote">
       <p>
        <i>
         Este neñín que teño nel collo
        </i>
        <br/>
       </p>
       <p>
        <i>
         e d'un amor que se tyama Vitorio,
        </i>
        <br/>
        <i>
         Dios que madeu, treveme llongo
        </i>
        <br/>
       </p>
       <i>
        por non andar con Vitorio nel collo.
       </i>
       <div class="templatequotecite">
        —
        <cite>
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Garc%C3%ADa_Lorca" title="García Lorca">
          García Lorca
         </a>
         , Las nanas infantiles
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36">
          <a href="#cite_note-36">
           [36]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </cite>
       </div>
      </blockquote>
      <p>
       (Navia)
      </p>
      <blockquote class="templatequote">
       <p>
        <i>
         As laxas d'a nosa entrada tan, madeus, muito moyadas, non miou mia sogra por elas e que anuncian a xelada
        </i>
        <br/>
        <i>
         Poderan ser cuadradas y tamén alongadas mais nunca veredes cocías redondiadas
        </i>
       </p>
       <div class="templatequotecite">
        —
        <cite>
         Labandera Campoamor, JA; Boletín de letras del Real Instituto de Estudios Asturianos nº 71, 1970,

      <p>
       (River Eo)
      </p>
      <blockquote class="templatequote">
       <p>
        <i>
         Ayer dicícheme c'hoy
        </i>
        <br/>
        <i>
         hoy dicesme que mañá
        </i>
        <br/>
        <i>
         y mañá as me decir
        </i>
        <br/>
        <i>
         ¿Cocéronxe xa as patacas?
        </i>
        <br/>
        <i>
         - Non: pero eiyes atizar candela -
        </i>
       </p>
       <div class="templatequotecite">
        —
        <cite>
         Sela García, Alejandro; Artículo publicado en el Aldeano, 2º semestre, Castropol 1932.
        </cite>
       </div>
      </blockquote>
      <blockquote class="templatequote">
       <p>
        <i>
         Vaich'a fer muito bèn
        </i>
        <br/>
       </p>
       <p>
        <i>
         Tèdes que vir a fèsta
        </i>
        <br/>
        <i>
         ¿Pareceche que fòron us nenos, us lladrois ou us parcoteixos us que tiraron as patacas al alto?
        </i>
        <br/>
        <i>
         ¿Sachasche el hòrto, atendich'as vacas ou fixich'a xanta?
        </i>
        <br/>
        <i>
         Fun al eiro, pero nun puiden sachar nada?
        </i>
        <br/>
        <i>
         Teis que ter ma(i)s tempo al fougo, parecem'a min esa caldeira.
        </i>
        <br/>
        <i>
         De recoyeredes entre us dous, el herba, è fácil que nun vola piye'l augua
        </i>
        <br/>
        <i>
         Tèinch'ua búa chía de d'herba
        </i>
        <br/>
        <i>
         Vid'a mía casa pra miraremos esos llibros
        </i>
        <br/>
        <i>
         Xa verás como en chegando`l vrao, imos a'ndar de fèsta'n fèsta
        </i>
        <br/>
        <i>
         Nun vos quèro delante, iscai xa!
        </i>
       </p>
       <div class="templatequotecite">
        —
        <cite>
         García García, José. (1983)
         <i>
          El habla de El Franco
         </i>
         , Bernaldo de Quiros 1.983
        </cite>
       </div>
      </blockquote>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Variants_according_to_ALPI">
        Variants according to ALPI
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Galician-Asturian&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Variants according to ALPI">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>

         </span>
        </td>
