      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Literature">
        Literature
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Galician-Asturian&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Literature">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Castropol_Newspaper_Cover.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="824" data-file-width="1508" height="137" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Castropol_Newspaper_Cover.jpg/250px-Castropol_Newspaper_Cover.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Castropol_Newspaper_Cover.jpg/375px-Castropol_Newspaper_Cover.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Castropol_Newspaper_Cover.jpg/500px-Castropol_Newspaper_Cover.jpg 2x" width="250"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Castropol_Newspaper_Cover.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The Castropol newspaper was the first publication that systematically includes texts in eonavian.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The first known writer in Eonavian language perhaps could be
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Fernan_Soares_de_Qui%C3%B1ones&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Fernan Soares de Quiñones (page does not exist)">
        Fernan Soares de Quiñones
       </a>
       or
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Fernan_Soares_de_Qui%C3%B1ones&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Fernan Soares de Quiñones (page does not exist)">
        Quinhões dos cancioneiros
       </a>
       , a troubadour of the last third of the 13th century. He was the author of four songs of moral satire, known as
       <i>
        (
        <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=C%C3%A1ntigas_de_escarnio_y_maldecir&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Cántigas de escarnio y maldecir (page does not exist)">
         cántigas de escarnio y maldecir
        </a>
        )
       </i>
       . One of the
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=C%C3%A1ntigas&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Cántigas (page does not exist)">
        cántigas
       </a>
       relates, in ancient
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Galician-Portuguese_language" title="Galician-Portuguese language">
        Galician-Portuguese language
       </a>
       , to the "costumes" (manners) and "feituras" (facts) of the "Cavalon" (old horse), which tells the adventures of a nobleman who lived in Seville, and had come from
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Oscos_Region&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Oscos Region (page does not exist)">
        Oscos Region
       </a>
       in "Esturas" (
       <a href="/wiki/Asturias" title="Asturias">
        Asturias
       </a>
       ) on the border with Galicia. The verses are included in a "cántiga" that is within the theme of "escarnio" (ridicule) and "maldecir" (cursing) but with the impersonation which is typical of the
       <i>
        "Cántiga de amigo"
       </i>
       (friend song). Anyway, it seems that the reference to the knight of Oscos presents allegorical connotations to the origin of the Asturian knight that might be related with the type of speech used in the cantiga.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39">
        <a href="#cite_note-39">
         [39]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       After the arrival of the
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Castillian_Congregation&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Castillian Congregation (page does not exist)">
        Castillian Congregation
       </a>
       at the [monastery of Santa María de
       <a href="/wiki/Villanueva_de_Oscos" title="Villanueva de Oscos">
        Villanueva de Oscos
       </a>
       in 1511, the written record of the language ended until its resurgence in the late 19th century.
      </p>
      <p>
       In the early years of the 20th century was an identification with Galician, reflected in authors like
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Cotarelo_Valledor&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Cotarelo Valledor (page does not exist)">
        Cotarelo Valledor
       </a>
       and
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Antolin_Santos_Ferraria&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Antolin Santos Ferraria (page does not exist)">
        Antolin Santos Ferraria
       </a>
       , who wrote entirely in Galician. Fernandez and Fernandez and Bernardo Acevedo Huelves were the first authors who are aware of the peculiarities of this language. The latest one is usually attributed the first sonnet in this language:
       <i>
        "Vusté era un gran señor, Eu era un gran probe"
       </i>
       (You was a great lord, I was a large poor man). A poet contemporary of them was Ramón García González, (1870-1938), who showedthe influence of the modernist spirit, prevailing in the early 20th century. His best-known work is a long poem entitled
       <i>
        "El xardín"
       </i>
       . Another poet in that time was Villar Conrado Loza (Taramundi 1873-Tapia 1962), who focused on themes around migration, recurring theme in folk literature on the early 20th century.
      </p>
      <p>
       After the
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Civil_War" title="Spanish Civil War">
        Spanish Civil War
       </a>
       was a decline of the literature in Asturian Galician, which lost the identity features that were beginning to appear. Folk literature was mixing Galician and Castilian and tended to be anecdotic rather than purely literary. In the 1970s, thanks to the work of authors such as
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Damaso_Alonso" title="Damaso Alonso">
        Damaso Alonso
       </a>
       , writers of the western end of Asturia began to reaffirm the identity of their language, such as Manuel Garcia Sanchez, known Manolo Galano, particularly concerned about the popular culture of the region and published, in 1994, with Jacinto López Díaz
       <i>
        "Vocabulario da Roda"
       </i>
       and had published in 1984:
       <i>
        "Cuentos Parzamiques"
       </i>
       . He was a frequent contributor to the magazine Entrambasauguas and published, in 2005, a recast of twenty written contributions to the magazine in the book
       <i>
        "Vento d'outono"
       </i>
       . Beside them are some more recent authors as Xose Miguel Suarez (Mantaras, Tapia, 1965) and Xavier Frias Conde. The writers started their literary careers, from the philological study of the language albeit from very different perspectives.
      </p>
      <p>
       The difficulty of publishing books for an audience so small makes it most remarkable of all that the literature projects through various magazines of the region. The oldest magazine is "A Freita", which appeared in eleven numbers, a general magazine that started to being published in 1992. Among its contributors were writers like Benigno Fernandez Braña, Xan Castañeira, Xosé Maximo Fernandez Muniz, Adela Valledor Conde, etc. In 1995, the magazine attached a literary supplement, published to makes noticed to the authors of Eonavia in other formats, through a kind of less formal book.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40">
        <a href="#cite_note-40">
         [40]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Since 1996, the Department of Linguistics of Eo Navia has published the magazine "Entrabasauguas". Among the writers often to collaborating are
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Veiguela_Crisanto&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Veiguela Crisanto (page does not exist)">
        Veiguela Crisanto
       </a>
       (Vegadeo 1959), Alejandro Blanco Antunez, (Navia 1933), Teresa Lopez, (Boal 1950),
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Xoxe_Carlos_Alvarez_Blanco&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Xoxe Carlos Alvarez Blanco (page does not exist)">
        Xoxe Carlos Alvarez Blanco
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Xavier_Vilareyo&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Xavier Vilareyo (page does not exist)">
        Xavier Vilareyo
       </a>
       (Mieres 1967),
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Fredo_de_Carbexe&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Fredo de Carbexe (page does not exist)">
        Fredo de Carbexe
       </a>
       (El Franco 1967), etc.
      </p>
      <p>
       In theatre, there is some tradition like in Villar and Manuel Galano. Lately, old plays have been recovered: "Condo el cariño è de Verdá", a comedy released in 1936 by Association Armal, and "El tratto de FF Arias", premiered in Figueras in 1926.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Associations">
        Associations
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Galician-Asturian&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Associations">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       In the dialectal area are associations supporting each side, such as
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Asociaci%C3%B3n_Abertal&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Asociación Abertal (page does not exist)">
        Asociación Abertal
       </a>
       (defending the Galician theory) and
       <a href="/wiki/Xeira" title="Xeira">
        Xeira
       </a>
       or Fala Viva (defending the Asturian theory). Its protection and
       <a href="/wiki/Language_policy" title="Language policy">
        language policy
       </a>
       are the responsibility of the Asturian government and the
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Secretar%C3%ADa_Lling%C3%BC%C3%ADstica_del_Navia-Eo&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Secretaría Llingüística del Navia-Eo (page does not exist)">
        Secretaría Llingüística del Navia-Eo
       </a>
       , a division of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Academia_de_la_Llingua_Asturiana" title="Academia de la Llingua Asturiana">
        Academia de la Llingua Asturiana
       </a>
       responsible for the area. There are two different orthographies for Eonavian, the official one (more Asturian-like) as well as one made by the Mesa prá Defensa del Galego de Asturias (more Galician-like).
      </p>

          </span>
          <span class="reference-text">
           This type of construction, although less frequent, can be seen in Old Castilian as well, for example the book of the Cifar Knight, (approx. 1300) «bien se que vos pesa, pero conoçerle-hedes esta vegada mejoría". Separable times are documented in Castilian to the 18th century and are still preserved in Judeo-Sephardic; see, for example, Hanssen, Gramática histórica de la lengua castellana, (1913), Paris 1966, § 62.

            </a>
           </b>
          </span>
          <span class="reference-text">
           <span class="languageicon">
            (in Asturian)
           </span>
           See too «Informe sobre a fala ou gallego asturiano», publicado por la
           <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Academia_de_la_Lengua_Asturiana&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Academia de la Lengua Asturiana (page does not exist)">
            Academia de la Lengua Asturiana
           </a>
           en 2006, p. 31; Bechara, Evanildo, Moderna Gramática Portuguesa, 36ª edición, 2003, p. 161;
           <span class="languageicon">
            (in Galician)
           </span>
           Cidrás Escáneo, Francisco (1998): "Marcaxe preposicional do obxecto en galego. Emerxencia e vicisitudes dun proceso de gramaticalización sintáctica", in Dieter Kremer (ed.): Homenaxe a Ramón Lorenzo. Vigo: Galaxia, vol II: 569-580). Usually, the phenomenon is caused by simple ellipsis of the nominal forms.
          </span>
         </li>
         <li id="cite_note-31">
          <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
           <b>
            <a href="#cite_ref-31">
             ^
            </a>
           </b>
          </span>
          <span class="reference-text">
           Alvárez Castrillón, José Antonio,
           <i>
            Colección Diplomática del Monasterio de Santa María de Villanueva de Oscos
           </i>
           , Ridea, 2011, p. 33
          </span>
         </li>
         <li id="cite_note-32">
          <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
           <b>
            <a href="#cite_ref-32">
             ^
            </a>
           </b>
          </span>
          <span class="reference-text">
           <a class="external text" href="http://www.ridea.org/biblioteca/bidea/PDFs/022-07.pdf" rel="nofollow">
            «El convento benedictino de Villanueva de Ozcos» BIDEA nº 22, 1954
           </a>
          </span>
         </li>
         <li id="cite_note-33">
          <span class="mw-cite-backlink">

           </span>

          </span>
         </li>
         <li id="cite_note-TA102-06-34">
          <span class="mw-cite-backlink">

           </a>
          </span>
         </li>

              </i>
              indicate
              <a href="/wiki/Language_death" title="Language death">
               extinct languages
              </a>
             </li>
             <li>
              <b>
               Bold
              </b>
              indicates
              <a href="/wiki/List_of_languages_by_number_of_native_speakers" title="List of languages by number of native speakers">
               languages with more than 5 million speakers
              </a>
             </li>
             <li>

              <a href="/wiki/Variety_(linguistics)" title="Variety (linguistics)">

              </a>
